ENVIRONMENTAL AND SOCIAL MANAGEMENT AND MONITORING PLANS

Environmental and Social Management Plan (ESMP)

Environmental and Social Management Plans (ESMPs) and related site-specific plans are essential tools for
ensuring that irrigation rehabilitation projects are carried out sustainably, safely, and in compliance with
legal and policy frameworks. They provide a structured approach to identifying, mitigating, and monitoring
potential environmental and social (E&S) risks and impacts across all project phases. The main site-specific
plan required under the study are
    •   Occupational health and safety plan,
    •   Community health and safety plan including Traffic Management Plan,
    •   Site Rehabilitation and Restoration Plan
    •   Construction Waste Management Plan.
    •   SEA/SH action plan (inconsideration of the main Project GBV/SEA/SH Action plan)
    •   Security risk management plan (SMP) (Contextualizing the main Project SMP)
    •   Stakeholder consultation and engagement Plan (contextualizing the main Project SEP)
    •   Water use plan (particularly for groundwater-based projects and where water is critical in the basins)
    •   Integrated pest management plan (IPMP)
    •   Irrigation salinity management plan
    •   Environmental and Social Monitoring Plan
    •   CAPACITY DEVELOPMENT AND TRAINING
    •   ANALYSIS OF ALTERNATIVES AND DESIGN OPTIONS
    •   GRM AND STAKEHOLDER’S CONSULTATIONS
    •   ESIA IMPLEMENTATION SCHEDULE
    •   ESIA IMPLEMENTATION BUDGET
    •   CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
    •   Conclusions
    •   Recommendations
    •   Annex 1: Site specific Contractor E&S considerations for a Bidding document
    •   Annex 2. List of the Consultant’s Team
    •   Annex 3: Records of Stakeholders Consultations
    •   Annex 4: References
Annex 13: Terms of Reference and Outline for Environmental and Social
Management Plan (ESMP)
BACKGROUND AND OBJECTIVE
The technical services of an independent environmental and social consultant (“Consultant”) are required
to prepare an Environmental and Social Management Plan (ESMP) for the CRISP Project.

The main objectives of the consultancy service are:
    - To identify the environmental and social impacts due to project implementation and operation.
    - To analyze, evaluate, and recommend measures to avoid, minimize, mitigate, and
       compensate/offset potential environmental and social impacts of the project so that it complies
       with the national, and World Bank’s Environmental and Social Standards (ESS), policies and
       frameworks.
    - To prepare environmental and social management and monitoring plans for implementation and
       operation phases of the project.

SCOPE OF WORK
In general, the Consultant will perform the following key tasks as part of the Environmental and Social
Management Plan (ESMP) preparation of the sub-project of the CRISP:

    -   Describe the sub-project including its main components, ancillary components/facilities,
        resources input, and outputs/produces.
    -   Identify project adverse environmental and social impacts and propose mitigation measures based
        on the mitigation hierarchy.
    -   Develop an environmental and social monitoring plan based on the mitigation plan developed.
    -   Assess the capacity of the implementing institution and recommend capacity development and
        training plan.
    -   Prepare implementation schedule and cost estimate for the ESMP implementation.

The details of the various activities of the ESMP are described in the below sections.

Introduction
The following key aspects of the sub-project should be defined and described.
    1. The Project background/context
    2. The specific sub-project background/context
    3. Rationale for the sub-project investment
    4. The objectives of the ESMP
    5. The scope of the ESMP
    6. Approach/methodology of the ESMP
    7. The structure of the ESMP report.


Project Description
The sub-project shall be described briefly including the following (but not limited to):
    - The location of the subproject (geographic and administrative locations)
    - Specific site location and key baseline conditions
    - Accessibility of the site
    -   The project intervention design and its main components/features
    -   Construction materials used for construction of various components of the project including
        sources of the construction materials (market or own source)
    -   Machineries to be used during construction and operation of the project
    -   Energy consumption for the project
    -   Waste generated by the project
    -   Human resources requirements during implementation and operation phases
    -   Project    implementation      activities   (during   pre-construction,  construction, and
        operation/maintenance stages)
    -   Project standard and regulatory requirements that should be maintained/satisfied
    -   Project implementation schedule.


Environnemental & Social Impacts Identification & Mitigation
As part of the ESMP preparation, the project adverse risks and impacts shall be identified, including
environmental risks, Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) risks, Community Health &Safety risks, Social
risks, labor-related risks, land and resettlement issues, risks related to development and operation of
ancillary facilities (if any).

The ESMP shall identify measures and actions in accordance with the mitigation hierarchy that reduce the
potential adverse environmental and social impacts to acceptable levels. The plan will include
compensatory measures, if applicable. Specifically, the ESMP shall:
    - Identify and summarize all anticipated adverse environmental and social impacts (including those
        involving indigenous people or involuntary resettlement).
    - Describe, with technical details, each mitigation measure, including the type of impact to which it
        relates and the conditions under which it is required (e.g., continuously or in the event of
        contingencies), together with designs, equipment descriptions, and operating procedures, as
        appropriate.
    - Estimate any potential environmental and social impacts of these measures.
    - Take into account, and consistent with, other mitigation plans required for the project (e.g., for
        involuntary resettlement, indigenous peoples, or cultural heritage).

A management plan shall be developed to implement the ESMP.

Monitoring
The ESMP shall identify monitoring objectives and specifies the type of monitoring, with linkages to the
impacts assessed in the environmental and social assessment and the mitigation measures described in
the ESMP. Specifically, the monitoring section of the ESMP provides (a) a specific description, and technical
details, of monitoring measures, including the parameters to be measured, methods to be used, sampling
locations, frequency of measurements, detection limits (where appropriate), and definition of thresholds
that will signal the need for corrective actions; and (b) monitoring and reporting procedures to (i) ensure
early detection of conditions that necessitate particular mitigation measures, and (ii) furnish information
on the progress and results of mitigation.

Capacity Development and Training
To support timely and effective implementation of environmental and social project components and
mitigation measures, the ESMP shall draw on the environmental and social assessment of the existence,
role, and capability of responsible parties on site or at the agency and ministry level.
Specifically, the ESMP shall provide a specific description of institutional arrangements, identifying which
party is responsible for carrying out the mitigation and monitoring measures (e.g., for operation,
supervision, enforcement, monitoring of implementation, remedial action, financing, reporting, and staff
training).

To strengthen environmental and social management capability in the agencies responsible for
implementation, the ESMP shall recommend the establishment or expansion of the parties responsible,
the training of staff and any additional measures that may be necessary to support implementation of
mitigation measures and any other recommendations of the environmental and social assessment.

Implementation Schedule and Cost Estimate
For all three aspects (mitigation, monitoring, and capacity development), the ESMP shall provide (a) an
implementation schedule for measures that must be carried out as part of the subproject, showing phasing
and coordination with overall project implementation plans; and (b) the capital and recurrent cost
estimates and sources of funds for implementing the ESMP. These figures shall also be integrated into the
total project cost tables.

 Integration of ESMP with the Project
Each of the measures and actions in the ESMP to be implemented shall be clearly specified, including the
individual mitigation and monitoring measures and actions and the institutional responsibilities relating
to each, and the costs of doing so shall be integrated into the subproject’s overall planning, design, budget,
implementation, and operation.

DELIVERABLES
The documents to be prepared as output of the consultancy service are Draft and Final Environmental and
Social Management Plans (ESMP). Detailed description and contents of the reports are presented in the
below sections. The deliverables shall be produced in English. The Consultant should prepare the draft and
final versions of the ESMP to the desired and acceptable quality to avoid several iterations of the plan.

INTEGRATION OF ESMP WITH THE PROJECT
Annex 14: Terms of Reference and Outline for Resettlement Action Plan
(RAP)
Background
The Government of Ethiopia, through the Ministry of Irrigation and Lowlands (MILLS) is implementing
the Climate Resilient Irrigation for Sustainable Production Irrigation (CRISP) Project in different regions of
Ethiopia. The project development objective (PDO) is to to improve access to resilient irrigation services
for sustainable production in Ethiopia.

The project involves land acquisition, restrictions on land use, and potential physical and/or economic
displacement in view of site-specific sub-projects. In accordance with the Ethiopian legal
framework (Proclamation No. 1161/2019 on Expropriation of Land for Public Purposes) and the World
Bank Environmental and Social Standard 5 (ESS5), a Resettlement Action Plan (RAP) must be prepared to
mitigate these impacts and ensure that Project Affected Persons (PAPs) are not left worse off as a result of
the project.

Objectives of the Assignment
The objective of this consultancy is to prepare a RAP that is:
    • Compliant with ESS5 and Ethiopian legal requirements.
    • Based on a census of displaced persons and inventory of affected assets.
    • Designed to provide fair, transparent, and adequate compensation, livelihood restoration, and
        resettlement support.
    • Inclusive, ensuring special attention to vulnerable and disadvantaged groups.
    • Implementable, with clear institutional arrangements, schedule, budget, and monitoring
        framework.

Scope of Work
The Consultant shall carry out the following:

    a) Legal and Institutional Review
    • Review national laws and regulations governing land acquisition, compensation, and resettlement.
    • Analyze gaps between Ethiopian laws and ESS5 requirements, and propose measures to bridge
       them.
    • Review institutional roles and capacities for RAP implementation.

    b) Socio-Economic Baseline and Census
    • Conduct a census of all Project Affected Persons (PAPs) to establish eligibility and prevent in-
       migration.
    • Carry out socio-economic household surveys to establish baseline conditions, including income
       sources, land use, tenure arrangements, and vulnerability status.
    • Identify vulnerable groups (e.g., women-headed households, elderly, landless, people with
       disabilities, minorities).

    c) Impact Assessment
    • Identify all project-induced land acquisition and restrictions on land use.
   •    Quantify impacts on households, assets (land, crops, structures), businesses, community facilities,
        and natural resources.
   •    Assess potential impacts on livelihoods, income streams, and social networks.

   d) Eligibility and Entitlements
   • Define categories of PAPs in line with ESS5 (those with legal rights to land, those without legal
      rights but with recognizable claims, and those without recognizable claims).
   • Develop an Entitlement Matrix, consistent with ESS5, covering compensation, assistance, and
      livelihood restoration.

   e) Resettlement and Livelihood Restoration Measures
   • Identify feasible resettlement site options (if physical relocation is necessary), ensuring adequate
      housing, infrastructure, and access to services.
   • Develop livelihood restoration programs, including agricultural support, vocational training,
      micro-enterprise opportunities, and employment linkages.
   • Propose special measures for vulnerable PAPs.

   f)   Stakeholder Engagement and Grievance Redress
   •    Prepare a Stakeholder Engagement Plan in line with ESS10, ensuring free, prior, and informed
        consultations.
   •    Design a Grievance Redress Mechanism (GRM), accessible to PAPs and tailored to local institutions
        and culture.

   g) Implementation Arrangements
   • Define roles and responsibilities of the Project Implementation Unit, woreda administrations, and
      other relevant stakeholders.
   • Provide a time-bound implementation schedule linked to the project construction timeline.
   • Prepare a cost estimate and budget for RAP implementation, including compensation, livelihood
      restoration, institutional strengthening, and monitoring.

   h)   Monitoring and Evaluation
   •    Develop internal and external monitoring arrangements.
   •    Propose indicators for tracking outputs, outcomes, and impacts of RAP implementation.
   •    Recommend third-party/independent monitoring if needed.

Deliverables
The Consultant shall deliver the following deliverables:
    1. Inception Report – methodology, detailed work plan, survey instruments.
    2. Draft RAP – covering all ESS5-required elements:
           a. Project description and impacts
           b. Census and baseline socio-economic data
           c. Legal and institutional framework
           d. Entitlement matrix and eligibility criteria
           e. Resettlement and livelihood restoration strategies
           f. Stakeholder engagement and GRM
           g. Implementation arrangements, schedule, and budget
           h. Monitoring and evaluation framework
    3. Consultation Report – documenting PAP and stakeholder engagement.
    4. Final RAP – incorporating comments from the GoE, World Bank, and stakeholders.
    5. Non-technical Summary in local language(s) for disclosure to PAPs.

An outline for the RAP is listed in the Table below.

Consultant Team and Qualifications
The team should comprise specialists with experience in World Bank ESSs (specifically ESS5), Ethiopian
land acquisition frameworks, and resettlement planning:
    • Team Leader/Resettlement Specialist (10+ years, ESS5 experience).
    • Sociologist/Anthropologist (socio-economic survey, community engagement).
    • Land Tenure/Legal Expert (Ethiopian expropriation law, customary tenure).

Duration
The assignment is expected to be completed within 2 months, allowing sufficient time for census, surveys,
consultations, and report preparation.

Reporting
The Consultant will report to the Project Implementation Unit (PIU) under MILLS, and coordinate closely
with woreda administrations and local authorities.
